        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer301755700" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3900586501655304888">I absolutely LOVED Edenbrooke. I won an ARC in a blog giveaway and cracked it open yesterday...I was immediately so captivated that I didn't want to put it down. I wasn't able to finish it in one sitting, but rather had to muster the self control to put it down in order to tend to my 21-month-old throughout the majority of the afternoon, but I immediately picked it up again after putting him to bed and read late into the night. I finished the book this morning and I can tell you that I was thoro</span>
  <span id="freeText3900586501655304888" style="display:none">I absolutely LOVED Edenbrooke. I won an ARC in a blog giveaway and cracked it open yesterday...I was immediately so captivated that I didn't want to put it down. I wasn't able to finish it in one sitting, but rather had to muster the self control to put it down in order to tend to my 21-month-old throughout the majority of the afternoon, but I immediately picked it up again after putting him to bed and read late into the night. I finished the book this morning and I can tell you that I was thoroughly pleased with the book in its entirety. There was not a dull moment to be had. I agree completely with what other readers have said...that the spirit of Jane Austen's beloved works was present throughout the entire novel (for those of you who LOVE Jane Austen as I do, it will not be difficult to see the reflection of her writing on the pages of this book). There were some parts that were so funny, that I literally laughed out loud (yes, at 1am, while I sat in my living room reading this morning). Other parts were so steamy (on a G-rated level of steam), that I could literally feel my heart pounding in my chest. The story is so immediately captivating, the characters so lovable...this has easily become the newest addition to my list of favorite books! It definitely left me wanting more. I am anxious for more of Julianne Donaldson's work to be published! :)</span>
  <a data-text-id="3900586501655304888" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_1655580723" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/1655580723" />
    <a title="Tito" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/21907583-tito"><img alt="Tito" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1475196819p2/21907583.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/1655580723?book_show_action=true">Jun 01, 2016</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Tito" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Tito" href="/user/show/21907583-tito">Tito</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21907583-tito?shelf=historical">historical</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21907583-tito?shelf=romance">romance</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21907583-tito?shelf=love-the-main-character-s">love-the-main-character-s</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21907583-tito?shelf=love-the-cover">love-the-cover</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21907583-tito?shelf=best-couples">best-couples</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21907583-tito?shelf=not-what-i-was-expecting">not-what-i-was-expecting</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21907583-tito?shelf=popular-author">popular-author</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21907583-tito?shelf=amazing-side-characters">amazing-side-characters</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21907583-tito?shelf=4-star">4-star</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/21907583-tito?shelf=lots-of-hype">lots-of-hype</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer1655580723" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer3296480550237409784">If I could describe this book in one word it would be cute. Honestly while reading I had the most <i>ridiculous</i> grin on my face the entire time. Most of it was because of the dialogue between Marianne and Phillip. Honestly, I have never read of a couple more perfect than these two, and they compliment each other really well. <br/><br/>Marianne's just a normal sweet 17 year old girl who doesn't really see herself as anything great compared to her sister, but as you read, you see that she's endearing, funny, a</span>
  <span id="freeText3296480550237409784" style="display:none">If I could describe this book in one word it would be cute. Honestly while reading I had the most <i>ridiculous</i> grin on my face the entire time. Most of it was because of the dialogue between Marianne and Phillip. Honestly, I have never read of a couple more perfect than these two, and they compliment each other really well. <br /><br />Marianne's just a normal sweet 17 year old girl who doesn't really see herself as anything great compared to her sister, but as you read, you see that she's endearing, funny, and incredibly brave. She's also really witty, and doesn't want to be like all the elegant and refined ladies in London. Instead she simply wants to be herself (and that includes having lots of freckles, walking around without a bonnet, and twirling. You just <i>have</i> to love the twirling), which is one of the biggest reasons why both I <i>and</i> Phillip like her. And <i>Phillip</i>! Goodness he's just as sweet as Marianne, and like her, he wants to be loved and appreciated for who he is, not for his money, which I thought was really nice. The romance for me was well played out because it didn't really rest on a lot of physical attraction. Instead they loved each other based on their personalities and that was very refreshing. What also made me smile about their relationship was the fact that Marianne was really oblivious to the fact that Phillip had a thing for her. I mean after the <a class="jsShowSpoiler spoilerAction">(view spoiler)</a><span class="spoilerContainer" style="display: none">[love letter, I was <i>sure</i> they would finally be a couple. But <i>alas</i>, no. It took stubborn Marianne a bit longer to understand <a class="jsHideSpoiler spoilerAction">(hide spoiler)</a>]</span>. <br /><br />I felt like the secondary characters were a nice addition to the story, although I must admit I loved Marianne's grandmother the best. She's the kind of person who seems rough on the outside, but inside, she's a real softie. <br /><br />Honestly, I just loved everything about this book, and can't wait to try out some other Julianne Donaldson books. Four stars for me!</span>
  <a data-text-id="3296480550237409784" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2075646333" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2075646333" />
    <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt"><img alt="Jacob Proffitt" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1325699498p2/1331641.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2075646333?book_show_action=true">Mar 21, 2019</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Jacob Proffitt" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Jacob Proffitt" href="/user/show/1331641-jacob-proffitt">Jacob Proffitt</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="did not like it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">did not like it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=will-probably-regret">will-probably-regret</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=negative-motivation">negative-motivation</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/1331641-jacob-proffitt?shelf=unfinished">unfinished</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2075646333" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer10854242318954700935">I do not get the popularity of this book. Marianne annoys the stuffing out of me and I can't get past her bone-deep stupidity. What six year-old carries a grudge against a <em>doll</em> and won't even <em>touch it with her bare fingers even though nobody is around</em> some eleven years later? A mentally deranged one, that's who. Marianne has taken a single instance of her twin, Cecily, getting her way and magnified it into pre-planned self-defeat in <em>every aspect of her life</em>. I don't find this sympathetic. I don'</span>
  <span id="freeText10854242318954700935" style="display:none">I do not get the popularity of this book. Marianne annoys the stuffing out of me and I can't get past her bone-deep stupidity. What six year-old carries a grudge against a <em>doll</em> and won't even <em>touch it with her bare fingers even though nobody is around</em> some eleven years later? A mentally deranged one, that's who. Marianne has taken a single instance of her twin, Cecily, getting her way and magnified it into pre-planned self-defeat in <em>every aspect of her life</em>. I don't find this sympathetic. I don't find it realistic, either, but if I <em>am</em> going to take it seriously then it is, at best, a seriously cowardly way to live your life and makes Marianne a weak and/or stupid girl.<br /><br />And what kind of sick mother lets this self-negating behavior continue in her daughter without lifting a hand to do anything about it?!? Marianne is all venerating her dead mother and talks/thinks about her constantly some fourteen months after her death and I'm all "girl, that woman left you to the tender mercies of your domineering jerk of a sister your entire life!" (I'm assuming that her sister is a selfish jerkwad. She was in the single scene I could tolerate once she showed up in the story). Mom's love, if she were capable of it, was a shallow and negligible thing. At best.<br /><br />Marianne is young so I can excuse some of these stupidities. But add in an addiction to "twirling" (srsly? She's 17 for heaven's sake!) and an emotional seesaw that rockets back and forth like it's the only toy in the only daycare in a city of toddlers and I'm just not feeling this. I know I can have idiosyncratic reactions to books, sometimes. But I truly do not get the popularity of this simpering simpleton and the boy who can't be bothered to make a simple statement of intent to the only girl who actually likes him for himself.</span>
  <a data-text-id="10854242318954700935" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_242383944" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/242383944" />
    <a title="Fred Donaldson" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/3239563-fred-donaldson"><img alt="Fred Donaldson" src="https://s.gr-assets.com/assets/nophoto/user/m_50x66-82093808bca726cb3249a493fbd3bd0f.png" /></a>

<span id="freeTextContainer17738676286188725440">I don't really read romance novels, so I lack a frame of reference. Edenbrooke tells an exciting regency story while giving insights into the main character. I stayed up really late in order to finish the second half of the book. It really is like nothing I have ever read--in a good way. This book is special.</span>

    <div class="section">
      

<div id="review_308379014" class="review nosyndicate" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/308379014" />
    <a title="Cathy" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/1327296-cathy"><img alt="Cathy" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1367714225p2/1327296.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/308379014?book_show_action=true">Apr 07, 2012</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Cathy" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Cathy" href="/user/show/1327296-cathy">Cathy</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="it was amazing"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">it was amazing</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span></span>



        

    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer308379014" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer7727767572001311773">One of my favorite books of all time! I can't believe I just said that. But I haven't stayed up all night reading a book in a VERY long time. This one did it to me. Why? Donaldson hints at some of it herself in the Q & A section at the back of the book. She loves the Regency Era, (who doesn't) but she wanted to make it more accessible to modern readers, so she eliminated the sometimes entangled 1800's language and kept it simple. She also streamlined the plot for accessibility, leaving out the s</span>
  <span id="freeText7727767572001311773" style="display:none">One of my favorite books of all time! I can't believe I just said that. But I haven't stayed up all night reading a book in a VERY long time. This one did it to me. Why? Donaldson hints at some of it herself in the Q &amp; A section at the back of the book. She loves the Regency Era, (who doesn't) but she wanted to make it more accessible to modern readers, so she eliminated the sometimes entangled 1800's language and kept it simple. She also streamlined the plot for accessibility, leaving out the social criticism found in Austen and Dickins. (See below) It is shorter, with 258 pages, and an easy read. But that wouldn't keep me up all night, surely. Nope. Once again, I can blame it on, that darned sooo effective, naive 1st Person narrator, which produces so much Dramatic Irony. Marianne is such an endearing doofus. We all see clearly, as do all the other characters, what she does not. He loves her, even as she insults his "Gentleman-liness", or he sees her twirl right into the muddy river or grasping tree branches that catch her hair, which Sir Phillip has to untangle. Embarrassing, great HUMOR. Great characters help too. The heroine is a noble, good character, one easy to empathize with. She underrates herself, is self-sacrificing, moral, loyal,- this is beginning to sound like the Boy Scout Code of Honor so I'll stop. Of all the Regency heroines,- this one is one we want to be like. She's not the stupid Emma - "Poorly done Emma, poorly done." Nor the easily taken in Marianne, nor Elinor, the sensible sister in Sense &amp; Sensibility. She is 17, childlike, and likeable. Sir Phillip is likewise honorable, noble, desirable, etc. But the thing that kept me up all night reading is the Perfect Pure ROMANCE! When Sir Phillip "teaches" Marianne how to write a love letter, a lesson in Romance, we KNOW, and Marianne suspects (Duh) that he might be writing these luscious, love words to and for HER!!! It is just Great! Best part of the book! I am sooo pleased that Donaldson read all the Georgette Heyer Regency romances after the Austen novels. Both writers set such a high standard or characterization, plot and theme, and I think Donaldson meets that standard, and shapes it to the 21st century. The reader will see shades of the other writers' characters in Donaldsons: The snootiness of P. &amp; P's Mr. Bingley's sister in some of the "elegant Ladies" Marianne is supposed to emulate. The abduction is so like Heyer's Regency Buck 1st scenes. Marianne's expression of joy in twirling so much like the release when Mr. Darcy and Miss Bennett in P. &amp; P. finally admit their joy in each other. What Austen (and Dickins) does, that Donaldson doesn't, is pick 19th Century social issues, such as women who can't inherit (S. &amp; S.), or unwed mothers whose orphaned children end up as street urchins. (Oliver) Donaldson veers far away from any criticism of the Time and its social structures. That's okay. But certainly doesn't push this novel into the "Classic"-must-read-in-AP-Classes" level. What the genius is is that ever present RESTRAINT of emotion and of lust (except in the most despicable) which builds such great tension and longing. When finally tears flow from the heroine, yours will too. I am so pleased that in the acknowledgements the author makes at the end of the book, she thanks God for his help and hope He is pleased. I think He is. We are!!!</span>
  <a data-text-id="7727767572001311773" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

          </span>
        </div>

<div id="review_2437487146" class="review" itemprop="reviews" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Review">
  <link itemprop="url" href="https://www.goodreads.com/review/show/2437487146" />
    <a title="Luisa Knight" class="left imgcol" href="/user/show/66567613-luisa-knight"><img alt="Luisa Knight" src="https://images.gr-assets.com/users/1491521288p2/66567613.jpg" /></a>

  <div class="left bodycol">
    <div class="reviewHeader uitext stacked">
        <a class="reviewDate createdAt right" href="/review/show/2437487146?book_show_action=true">Aug 31, 2018</a>

      <span itemprop="author" itemscope itemtype="http://schema.org/Person">
        <a title="Luisa Knight" class="user" itemprop="url" name="Luisa Knight" href="/user/show/66567613-luisa-knight">Luisa Knight</a>
      </span>

        rated it
        <span class=" staticStars notranslate" title="really liked it"><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10">really liked it</span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p10"></span><span size="15x15" class="staticStar p0"></span></span>



        

          <div class="uitext greyText bookshelves">
            Shelves:
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66567613-luisa-knight?shelf=audible">audible</a>, 
              <a class="actionLinkLite" href="/review/list/66567613-luisa-knight?shelf=romance">romance</a>
          </div>
    </div>


        <div class="reviewText stacked">
              <span id="reviewTextContainer2437487146" class="readable"
              >
            
<span id="freeTextContainer4062641610294871735">This title will definitely stand out in this year's reading. I thoroughly enjoyed it!<br/><br/>It has just the right mixture of everything: think Jane Austen era, hilarious Anne Shirley catastrophes, a flirty and romantic Hallmark male lead and some action sequences from which the leading lady must be rescued. Though admittedly cliche sounding, you truly won't be able to resist this really well constructed story. I guarantee it! I had a hard time putting it down. <br/><br/>Just don't listen to the audio like I did.</span>
  <span id="freeText4062641610294871735" style="display:none">This title will definitely stand out in this year's reading. I thoroughly enjoyed it!<br /><br />It has just the right mixture of everything: think Jane Austen era, hilarious Anne Shirley catastrophes, a flirty and romantic Hallmark male lead and some action sequences from which the leading lady must be rescued. Though admittedly cliche sounding, you truly won't be able to resist this really well constructed story. I guarantee it! I had a hard time putting it down. <br /><br />Just don't listen to the audio like I did. It was agonizingly horrid. But perhaps you like a fake sounding British accent spoken in a sickly sweet fashion. If you do, by all means ...<br /><br />Cleanliness: Mentions wine, brandy and a drunk. Mentions gambling and betting on horse races. There is a robbery and two people are injured - not gory. There is an attempted/an abduction of a young lady; her abductor kisses her (barely detailed) and wishes to force a marriage (as she will be thought of as "damaged goods") to gain her wealth. There are a few kisses which are not very detailed - one is. There is an urge to kiss a man and several instances of touching (hands, shoulder, chin, strand of hair) which cause some chills/shivers - semi-detailed. There is a lot of flirting and blushing. Two female side characters are often talking about or are kissing "rakes" (men who are not thought of as proper but ones that "know how to kiss.") - the main character is laughed at because she does not want to take part and thinks it's awful. Two men are mistakenly thought to be off carousing and seeking pleasure through conquests (sexually) - they are not and there are no details. <br /><br />*Note: I listened to the audio version of this book so this Cleanliness Report may not be as thoroughly detailed as other reports are. Also, some inappropriate content may have been forgotten/missed and not included in the report.<br /><br />**Like my reviews? Then you should follow me! Because I have hundreds more just like this one. With each review, I provide a Cleanliness Report, mentioning any objectionable content I come across so that parents and/or conscientious readers (like me) can determine beforehand whether they want to read a book or not. Content surprises are super annoying, especially when you’re 100+ pages in, so here’s my attempt to help you avoid that! <br /><br />So Follow or Friend me here on GoodReads! You’ll see my updates as I’m reading and know which books I’m liking and what I’m not finishing and why. You’ll also be able to utilize my library for looking up titles to see whether the book you’re thinking about reading next has any objectionable content or not. From swear words, to romance, to bad attitudes (in children’s books), I cover it all!<br /></span>
  <a data-text-id="4062641610294871735" href="#" onclick="swapContent($(this));; return false;">...more</a>

  function submitShelfLink(unique_id, book_id, shelf_id, shelf_name, submit_form, exclusive) {
    var checkbox_id = 'shelf_name_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    var element = document.getElementById(checkbox_id)

    var checked = element.checked
    if (checked && exclusive) {
      // can't uncheck a radio by clicking it!
      return
    }
    if(document.getElementById("savingMessage")){
      Element.show('savingMessage')
    }
    var element_id = 'shelfInDropdownName_' + unique_id + '_' + shelf_id;
    Element.update(element_id, "saving...");
    if (submit_form) {
      Element.hide('shelfDropdown_' + unique_id)
      var form = document.getElementById('addBookForm' + book_id)
      if (form) {
        form.shelf.value = shelf_name
        form.onsubmit()
      }
    }
    else {
      var action = checked ? 'remove' : ''
      element.checked = !element.checked
      new Ajax.Request('/shelf/add_to_shelf', {asynchronous:true, evalScripts:true, onSuccess:function(request){shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name)}, parameters:'book_id=' + book_id + '&name=' + shelf_name + '&a=' + action + '&authenticity_token=' + encodeURIComponent('xGmCCKhADb2Gl0MdDDFQqmzOcX7BGHoK4mJ1vM2pFEN7/s2uV4rCZl2vsJGyjEyMHkul0mESFc8/Xw58uyXVyA==')})
    }
  }

  function shelfSubmitted(request, book_id, checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name) {
    Element.update('shelfListfalse_' + book_id, request.responseText)
    afterShelfSave(checkbox_id, element_id, unique_id, shelf_name.escapeHTML())
  }

  function refreshGroupBox(group_id, book_id) {

  }

<div class='bookAuthorProfile__about'>

<span id="freeTextContainer1990707954617556701">Julianne Donaldson grew up as the daughter of a U.S. Air Force fighter pilot. She learned how to ski in the Italian Alps, visited East Berlin before the wall came down, and spent three years living next to a 500-year-old castle. After earning a degree in English, she turned her attention to writing. She writes historical romance when she is not busy with her four young children and husband. Edenbr</span>
  <span id="freeText1990707954617556701" style="display:none">Julianne Donaldson grew up as the daughter of a U.S. Air Force fighter pilot. She learned how to ski in the Italian Alps, visited East Berlin before the wall came down, and spent three years living next to a 500-year-old castle. After earning a degree in English, she turned her attention to writing. She writes historical romance when she is not busy with her four young children and husband. Edenbrooke is her first novel.</span>

Your blindness to my feelings is a daily torment, and I feel driven to the edge of madness by my love for you.<br />Where is your compassion when I need it most?
